# Simple but Powerful Pratt Parsing from Matklad
<details open="true">
<summary>Expand to view code</summary>
<pre className="cire"><code>
<span className="keyword">{`use`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ std`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`::`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`fmt`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ io`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`::`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">trait</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">BufRead</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">where</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="bp">Self</span>: <span class="nc">Read</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>A <code>BufRead</code> is a type of <code>Read</code>er which has an internal buffer, allowing it<br>
to perform extra ways of reading.</p>
<p>For example, reading line-by-line is inefficient without using a buffer, so<br>
if you want to read by line, you'll need <code>BufRead</code>, which includes a<br>
[<code>read_line</code>] method as well as a [<code>lines</code>] iterator.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<p>A locked standard input implements <code>BufRead</code>:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">prelude</span>::<span class="o">*</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">stdin</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">stdin</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">line</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">stdin</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">lock</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">lines</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">line</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>If you have something that implements <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/trait.Read.html"><code>Read</code></a>, you can use the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/buffered/bufreader/struct.BufReader.html"><code>BufReader</code><br>
type</a> to turn it into a <code>BufRead</code>.</p>
<p>For example, [<code>File</code>] implements <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/trait.Read.html"><code>Read</code></a>, but not <code>BufRead</code>.<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/buffered/bufreader/struct.BufReader.html"><code>BufReader</code></a> to the rescue!</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">BufReader</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">prelude</span>::<span class="o">*</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fs</span>::<span class="n">File</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">io</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">f</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">File</span>::<span class="n">open</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;foo.txt&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">f</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">BufReader</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">f</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">line</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">f</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">lines</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">        </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">line</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">line</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">        </span><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{line}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="constructor">{`BufRead`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`;`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

`}</span><span className="keyword">{`enum`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_10_5" className="type">{`S`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span>::<span class="n">S</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">Atom</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>size = 12 (0xC), align = 0x4, no Drop</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_11_4" className="constructor">{`Atom`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">char</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>A character type.</p>
<p>The <code>char</code> type represents a single character. More specifically, since<br>
'character' isn't a well-defined concept in Unicode, <code>char</code> is a '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#unicode_scalar_value">Unicode<br>
scalar value</a>'.</p>
<p>This documentation describes a number of methods and trait implementations on the<br>
<code>char</code> type. For technical reasons, there is additional, separate<br>
documentation in <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/char/index.html">the <code>std::char</code> module</a> as well.</p>
<h1 id="validity-and-layout">Validity and Layout</h1>
<p>A <code>char</code> is a '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#unicode_scalar_value">Unicode scalar value</a>', which is any '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#code_point">Unicode code point</a>'<br>
other than a <a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_code_point">surrogate code point</a>. This has a fixed numerical definition:<br>
code points are in the range 0 to 0x10FFFF, inclusive.<br>
Surrogate code points, used by UTF-16, are in the range 0xD800 to 0xDFFF.</p>
<p>No <code>char</code> may be constructed, whether as a literal or at runtime, that is not a<br>
Unicode scalar value. Violating this rule causes undefined behavior.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Each of these is a compiler error
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{D800}&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{DFFF}&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{110000}&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Panics; from_u32 returns None.
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">from_u32</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mh">0xDE01</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">unwrap</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Undefined behavior
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">unsafe</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">from_u32_unchecked</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mh">0x110000</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Unicode scalar values are also the exact set of values that may be encoded in UTF-8. Because<br>
<code>char</code> values are Unicode scalar values and functions may assume <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/primitive.str.html#invariant">incoming <code>str</code> values are<br>
valid UTF-8</a>, it is safe to store any <code>char</code> in a <code>str</code> or read<br>
any character from a <code>str</code> as a <code>char</code>.</p>
<p>The gap in valid <code>char</code> values is understood by the compiler, so in the<br>
below example the two ranges are understood to cover the whole range of<br>
possible <code>char</code> values and there is no error for a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/book/ch06-02-match.html#matches-are-exhaustive">non-exhaustive match</a>.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">c</span>: <span class="kt">char</span> <span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;a&#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">match</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">c</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\0&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">..=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{D7FF}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">false</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{E000}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">..=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{10FFFF}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">true</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>All Unicode scalar values are valid <code>char</code> values, but not all of them represent a real<br>
character. Many Unicode scalar values are not currently assigned to a character, but may be in<br>
the future (&quot;reserved&quot;); some will never be a character (&quot;noncharacters&quot;); and some may be given<br>
different meanings by different users (&quot;private use&quot;).</p>
<p><code>char</code> is guaranteed to have the same size, alignment, and function call ABI as <code>u32</code> on all<br>
platforms.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">Layout</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">Layout</span>::<span class="n">new</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Layout</span>::<span class="n">new</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><h1 id="representation">Representation</h1>
<p><code>char</code> is always four bytes in size. This is a different representation than<br>
a given character would have as part of a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/string/struct.String.html"><code>String</code></a>. For example:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;h&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;e&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;l&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;l&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;o&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// five elements times four bytes for each element
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">20</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;hello&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// five elements times one byte per element
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>As always, remember that a human intuition for 'character' might not map to<br>
Unicode's definitions. For example, despite looking similar, the 'é'<br>
character is one Unicode code point while 'é' is two Unicode code points:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;é&#34;</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+00e9: &#39;latin small letter e with acute&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{00e9}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;é&#34;</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+0065: &#39;latin small letter e&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{0065}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+0301: &#39;combining acute accent&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{0301}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>This means that the contents of the first string above <em>will</em> fit into a<br>
<code>char</code> while the contents of the second string <em>will not</em>. Trying to create<br>
a <code>char</code> literal with the contents of the second string gives an error:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl">error: character literal may only contain one codepoint: &#39;é&#39;
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">let c = &#39;é&#39;;
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">        ^^^
</span></span></code></pre><p>Another implication of the 4-byte fixed size of a <code>char</code> is that<br>
per-<code>char</code> processing can end up using a lot more memory:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;love: ❤️&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span>: <span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">collect</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">12</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of_val</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="p">]));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">32</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of_val</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="p">]));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type.builtin">{`char`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span>::<span class="n">S</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">Cons</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">S</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>size = 32 (0x20), align = 0x8, needs Drop</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_12_4" className="constructor">{`Cons`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">char</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>A character type.</p>
<p>The <code>char</code> type represents a single character. More specifically, since<br>
'character' isn't a well-defined concept in Unicode, <code>char</code> is a '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#unicode_scalar_value">Unicode<br>
scalar value</a>'.</p>
<p>This documentation describes a number of methods and trait implementations on the<br>
<code>char</code> type. For technical reasons, there is additional, separate<br>
documentation in <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/char/index.html">the <code>std::char</code> module</a> as well.</p>
<h1 id="validity-and-layout">Validity and Layout</h1>
<p>A <code>char</code> is a '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#unicode_scalar_value">Unicode scalar value</a>', which is any '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#code_point">Unicode code point</a>'<br>
other than a <a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_code_point">surrogate code point</a>. This has a fixed numerical definition:<br>
code points are in the range 0 to 0x10FFFF, inclusive.<br>
Surrogate code points, used by UTF-16, are in the range 0xD800 to 0xDFFF.</p>
<p>No <code>char</code> may be constructed, whether as a literal or at runtime, that is not a<br>
Unicode scalar value. Violating this rule causes undefined behavior.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Each of these is a compiler error
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{D800}&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{DFFF}&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{110000}&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Panics; from_u32 returns None.
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">from_u32</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mh">0xDE01</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">unwrap</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Undefined behavior
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">unsafe</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">from_u32_unchecked</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mh">0x110000</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Unicode scalar values are also the exact set of values that may be encoded in UTF-8. Because<br>
<code>char</code> values are Unicode scalar values and functions may assume <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/primitive.str.html#invariant">incoming <code>str</code> values are<br>
valid UTF-8</a>, it is safe to store any <code>char</code> in a <code>str</code> or read<br>
any character from a <code>str</code> as a <code>char</code>.</p>
<p>The gap in valid <code>char</code> values is understood by the compiler, so in the<br>
below example the two ranges are understood to cover the whole range of<br>
possible <code>char</code> values and there is no error for a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/book/ch06-02-match.html#matches-are-exhaustive">non-exhaustive match</a>.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">c</span>: <span class="kt">char</span> <span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;a&#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">match</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">c</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\0&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">..=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{D7FF}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">false</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{E000}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">..=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{10FFFF}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">true</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>All Unicode scalar values are valid <code>char</code> values, but not all of them represent a real<br>
character. Many Unicode scalar values are not currently assigned to a character, but may be in<br>
the future (&quot;reserved&quot;); some will never be a character (&quot;noncharacters&quot;); and some may be given<br>
different meanings by different users (&quot;private use&quot;).</p>
<p><code>char</code> is guaranteed to have the same size, alignment, and function call ABI as <code>u32</code> on all<br>
platforms.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">Layout</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">Layout</span>::<span class="n">new</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Layout</span>::<span class="n">new</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><h1 id="representation">Representation</h1>
<p><code>char</code> is always four bytes in size. This is a different representation than<br>
a given character would have as part of a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/string/struct.String.html"><code>String</code></a>. For example:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;h&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;e&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;l&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;l&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;o&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// five elements times four bytes for each element
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">20</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;hello&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// five elements times one byte per element
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>As always, remember that a human intuition for 'character' might not map to<br>
Unicode's definitions. For example, despite looking similar, the 'é'<br>
character is one Unicode code point while 'é' is two Unicode code points:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;é&#34;</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+00e9: &#39;latin small letter e with acute&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{00e9}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;é&#34;</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+0065: &#39;latin small letter e&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{0065}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+0301: &#39;combining acute accent&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{0301}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>This means that the contents of the first string above <em>will</em> fit into a<br>
<code>char</code> while the contents of the second string <em>will not</em>. Trying to create<br>
a <code>char</code> literal with the contents of the second string gives an error:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl">error: character literal may only contain one codepoint: &#39;é&#39;
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">let c = &#39;é&#39;;
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">        ^^^
</span></span></code></pre><p>Another implication of the 4-byte fixed size of a <code>char</code> is that<br>
per-<code>char</code> processing can end up using a lot more memory:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;love: ❤️&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span>: <span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">collect</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">12</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of_val</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="p">]));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">32</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of_val</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="p">]));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type.builtin">{`char`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">vec</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">A</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Global</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">where</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">A</span>: <span class="nc">Allocator</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">buf</span>: <span class="nc">RawVec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">A</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">len</span>: <span class="kt">usize</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>A contiguous growable array type, written as <code>Vec&lt;T&gt;</code>, short for 'vector'.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">pop</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">7</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">7</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">extend</span><span class="p">([</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{x}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">7</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>The <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/macros/macro.vec.html"><code>vec</code></a> macro is provided for convenient initialization:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec1</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec1</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec2</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">([</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>It can also initialize each element of a <code>Vec&lt;T&gt;</code> with a given value.<br>
This may be more efficient than performing allocation and initialization<br>
in separate steps, especially when initializing a vector of zeros:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// The following is equivalent, but potentially slower:
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">with_capacity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">resize</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>For more information, see<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/vec/struct.Vec.html#capacity-and-reallocation">Capacity and Reallocation</a>.</p>
<p>Use a <code>Vec&lt;T&gt;</code> as an efficient stack:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">stack</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">stack</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">stack</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">stack</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">while</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">top</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">stack</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">pop</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="c1">// Prints 3, 2, 1
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{top}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><h1 id="indexing">Indexing</h1>
<p>The <code>Vec</code> type allows access to values by index, because it implements the<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/ops/index/trait.Index.html"><code>Index</code></a> trait. An example will be more explicit:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// it will display &#39;2&#39;
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>However be careful: if you try to access an index which isn't in the <code>Vec</code>,<br>
your software will panic! You cannot do this:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// it will panic!
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Use [<code>get</code>] and [<code>get_mut</code>] if you want to check whether the index is in<br>
the <code>Vec</code>.</p>
<h1 id="slicing">Slicing</h1>
<p>A <code>Vec</code> can be mutable. On the other hand, slices are read-only objects.<br>
To get a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/slice/index.html">slice</a>, use <a href="%60&amp;%60"><code>&amp;</code></a>. Example:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">read_slice</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">slice</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="kt">usize</span><span class="p">])</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="c1">// ...
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">read_slice</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// ... and that&#39;s all!
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// you can also do it like this:
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">u</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="kt">usize</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// or like this:
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">u</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>In Rust, it's more common to pass slices as arguments rather than vectors<br>
when you just want to provide read access. The same goes for [<code>String</code>] and<br>
[<code>&amp;str</code>].</p>
<h1 id="capacity-and-reallocation">Capacity and reallocation</h1>
<p>The capacity of a vector is the amount of space allocated for any future<br>
elements that will be added onto the vector. This is not to be confused with<br>
the <em>length</em> of a vector, which specifies the number of actual elements<br>
within the vector. If a vector's length exceeds its capacity, its capacity<br>
will automatically be increased, but its elements will have to be<br>
reallocated.</p>
<p>For example, a vector with capacity 10 and length 0 would be an empty vector<br>
with space for 10 more elements. Pushing 10 or fewer elements onto the<br>
vector will not change its capacity or cause reallocation to occur. However,<br>
if the vector's length is increased to 11, it will have to reallocate, which<br>
can be slow. For this reason, it is recommended to use <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/vec/struct.Vec.html#method.with_capacity"><code>Vec::with_capacity</code></a><br>
whenever possible to specify how big the vector is expected to get.</p>
<h1 id="guarantees">Guarantees</h1>
<p>Due to its incredibly fundamental nature, <code>Vec</code> makes a lot of guarantees<br>
about its design. This ensures that it's as low-overhead as possible in<br>
the general case, and can be correctly manipulated in primitive ways<br>
by unsafe code. Note that these guarantees refer to an unqualified <code>Vec&lt;T&gt;</code>.<br>
If additional type parameters are added (e.g., to support custom allocators),<br>
overriding their defaults may change the behavior.</p>
<p>Most fundamentally, <code>Vec</code> is and always will be a (pointer, capacity, length)<br>
triplet. No more, no less. The order of these fields is completely<br>
unspecified, and you should use the appropriate methods to modify these.<br>
The pointer will never be null, so this type is null-pointer-optimized.</p>
<p>However, the pointer might not actually point to allocated memory. In particular,<br>
if you construct a <code>Vec</code> with capacity 0 via <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/vec/struct.Vec.html#method.new"><code>Vec::new</code></a>, <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/macros/macro.vec.html"><code>vec![]</code></a>,<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/vec/struct.Vec.html#method.with_capacity"><code>Vec::with_capacity(0)</code></a>, or by calling [<code>shrink_to_fit</code>]<br>
on an empty Vec, it will not allocate memory. Similarly, if you store zero-sized<br>
types inside a <code>Vec</code>, it will not allocate space for them. <em>Note that in this case<br>
the <code>Vec</code> might not report a [<code>capacity</code>] of 0</em>. <code>Vec</code> will allocate if and only<br>
if <code><br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/mem/fn.size_of.html">size_of::&lt;T&gt;</a>() * <a href="">capacity</a> &gt; 0</code>. In general, <code>Vec</code>'s allocation<br>
details are very subtle --- if you intend to allocate memory using a <code>Vec</code><br>
and use it for something else (either to pass to unsafe code, or to build your<br>
own memory-backed collection), be sure to deallocate this memory by using<br>
<code>from_raw_parts</code> to recover the <code>Vec</code> and then dropping it.</p>
<p>If a <code>Vec</code> <em>has</em> allocated memory, then the memory it points to is on the heap<br>
(as defined by the allocator Rust is configured to use by default), and its<br>
pointer points to [<code>len</code>] initialized, contiguous elements in order (what<br>
you would see if you coerced it to a slice), followed by <code><br>
[capacity] - [len]</code><br>
logically uninitialized, contiguous elements.</p>
<p>A vector containing the elements <code>'a'</code> and <code>'b'</code> with capacity 4 can be<br>
visualized as below. The top part is the <code>Vec</code> struct, it contains a<br>
pointer to the head of the allocation in the heap, length and capacity.<br>
The bottom part is the allocation on the heap, a contiguous memory block.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl">            ptr      len  capacity
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">       +--------+--------+--------+
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">       | 0x0123 |      2 |      4 |
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">       +--------+--------+--------+
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">            |
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">            v
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">Heap   +--------+--------+--------+--------+
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">       |    &#39;a&#39; |    &#39;b&#39; | uninit | uninit |
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">       +--------+--------+--------+--------+
</span></span></code></pre><ul>
<li><strong>uninit</strong> represents memory that is not initialized, see [<code>MaybeUninit</code>].</li>
<li>Note: the ABI is not stable and <code>Vec</code> makes no guarantees about its memory<br>
layout (including the order of fields).</li>
</ul>
<p><code>Vec</code> will never perform a &quot;small optimization&quot; where elements are actually<br>
stored on the stack for two reasons:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It would make it more difficult for unsafe code to correctly manipulate<br>
a <code>Vec</code>. The contents of a <code>Vec</code> wouldn't have a stable address if it were<br>
only moved, and it would be more difficult to determine if a <code>Vec</code> had<br>
actually allocated memory.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It would penalize the general case, incurring an additional branch<br>
on every access.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><code>Vec</code> will never automatically shrink itself, even if completely empty. This<br>
ensures no unnecessary allocations or deallocations occur. Emptying a <code>Vec</code><br>
and then filling it back up to the same [<code>len</code>] should incur no calls to<br>
the allocator. If you wish to free up unused memory, use<br>
[<code>shrink_to_fit</code>] or [<code>shrink_to</code>].</p>
<p>[<code>push</code>] and [<code>insert</code>] will never (re)allocate if the reported capacity is<br>
sufficient. [<code>push</code>] and [<code>insert</code>] <em>will</em> (re)allocate if<br>
<code><br>
[len] == [capacity]</code>. That is, the reported capacity is completely<br>
accurate, and can be relied on. It can even be used to manually free the memory<br>
allocated by a <code>Vec</code> if desired. Bulk insertion methods <em>may</em> reallocate, even<br>
when not necessary.</p>
<p><code>Vec</code> does not guarantee any particular growth strategy when reallocating<br>
when full, nor when [<code>reserve</code>] is called. The current strategy is basic<br>
and it may prove desirable to use a non-constant growth factor. Whatever<br>
strategy is used will of course guarantee <em>O</em>(1) amortized [<code>push</code>].</p>
<p>It is guaranteed, in order to respect the intentions of the programmer, that<br>
all of <code>vec![e_1, e_2, ..., e_n]</code>, <code>vec![x; n]</code>, and [<code>Vec::with_capacity(n)</code>] produce a <code>Vec</code><br>
that requests an allocation of the exact size needed for precisely <code>n</code> elements from the allocator,<br>
and no other size (such as, for example: a size rounded up to the nearest power of 2).<br>
The allocator will return an allocation that is at least as large as requested, but it may be larger.</p>
<p>It is guaranteed that the [<code>Vec::capacity</code>] method returns a value that is at least the requested capacity<br>
and not more than the allocated capacity.</p>
<p>The method <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/vec/struct.Vec.html#method.shrink_to_fit"><code>Vec::shrink_to_fit</code></a> will attempt to discard excess capacity an allocator has given to a <code>Vec</code>.<br>
If <code><br>
[len] == [capacity]</code>, then a <code>Vec&lt;T&gt;</code> can be converted<br>
to and from a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/boxed/struct.Box.html"><code>Box&lt;[T]&gt;</code></a> without reallocating or moving the elements.<br>
<code>Vec</code> exploits this fact as much as reasonable when implementing common conversions<br>
such as [<code>into_boxed_slice</code>].</p>
<p><code>Vec</code> will not specifically overwrite any data that is removed from it,<br>
but also won't specifically preserve it. Its uninitialized memory is<br>
scratch space that it may use however it wants. It will generally just do<br>
whatever is most efficient or otherwise easy to implement. Do not rely on<br>
removed data to be erased for security purposes. Even if you drop a <code>Vec</code>, its<br>
buffer may simply be reused by another allocation. Even if you zero a <code>Vec</code>'s memory<br>
first, that might not actually happen because the optimizer does not consider<br>
this a side-effect that must be preserved. There is one case which we will<br>
not break, however: using <code>unsafe</code> code to write to the excess capacity,<br>
and then increasing the length to match, is always valid.</p>
<p>Currently, <code>Vec</code> does not guarantee the order in which elements are dropped.<br>
The order has changed in the past and may change again.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type">{`Vec`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`<`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">enum</span> <span class="nc">S</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Atom</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="cm">/* … */</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Cons</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="cm">/* … */</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_10_5" className="type">{`S`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`>`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

`}</span><span className="keyword">{`impl`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ fmt`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`::`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">trait</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Display</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">where</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="bp">Self</span>: <span class="nc">PointeeSized</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Format trait for an empty format, <code>{}</code>.</p>
<p>Implementing this trait for a type will automatically implement the<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/string/trait.ToString.html"><code>ToString</code></a> trait for the type, allowing the usage<br>
of the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/string/trait.ToString.html#tymethod.to_string"><code>.to_string()</code></a> method. Prefer implementing<br>
the <code>Display</code> trait for a type, rather than <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/string/trait.ToString.html"><code>ToString</code></a>.</p>
<p><code>Display</code> is similar to <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/fmt/trait.Debug.html"><code>Debug</code></a>, but <code>Display</code> is for user-facing<br>
output, and so cannot be derived.</p>
<p>For more information on formatters, see <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/fmt/index.html">the module-level documentation</a>.</p>
<h1 id="completeness-and-parseability">Completeness and parseability</h1>
<p><code>Display</code> for a type might not necessarily be a lossless or complete representation of the type.<br>
It may omit internal state, precision, or other information the type does not consider important<br>
for user-facing output, as determined by the type. As such, the output of <code>Display</code> might not be<br>
possible to parse, and even if it is, the result of parsing might not exactly match the original<br>
value.</p>
<p>However, if a type has a lossless <code>Display</code> implementation whose output is meant to be<br>
conveniently machine-parseable and not just meant for human consumption, then the type may wish<br>
to accept the same format in <code>FromStr</code>, and document that usage. Having both <code>Display</code> and<br>
<code>FromStr</code> implementations where the result of <code>Display</code> cannot be parsed with <code>FromStr</code> may<br>
surprise users.</p>
<h1 id="internationalization">Internationalization</h1>
<p>Because a type can only have one <code>Display</code> implementation, it is often preferable<br>
to only implement <code>Display</code> when there is a single most &quot;obvious&quot; way that<br>
values can be formatted as text. This could mean formatting according to the<br>
&quot;invariant&quot; culture and &quot;undefined&quot; locale, or it could mean that the type<br>
display is designed for a specific culture/locale, such as developer logs.</p>
<p>If not all values have a justifiably canonical textual format or if you want<br>
to support alternative formats not covered by the standard set of possible<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/fmt/index.html#formatting-traits">formatting traits</a>, the most flexible approach is display adapters: methods<br>
like <a href="%60str::escape_default%60"><code>str::escape_default</code></a> or <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/path/struct.Path.html#method.display"><code>Path::display</code></a> which create a wrapper<br>
implementing <code>Display</code> to output the specific display format.</p>

<p>Configuration for formatting.</p>
<p>A <code>Formatter</code> represents various options related to formatting. Users do not<br>
construct <code>Formatter</code>s directly; a mutable reference to one is passed to<br>
the <code>fmt</code> method of all formatting traits, like <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/fmt/trait.Debug.html"><code>Debug</code></a> and <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/fmt/trait.Display.html"><code>Display</code></a>.</p>
<p>To interact with a <code>Formatter</code>, you'll call various methods to change the<br>
various options related to formatting. For examples, please see the<br>
documentation of the methods defined on <code>Formatter</code> below.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type">{`Formatter`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`<`}</span><span className="operator">{`'`}</span><span className="label">{`_`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`>`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ ->\ fmt`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`::`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span><span class="w">
