</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_16_12" className="variable.builtin">{`self`}</a></Tooltip><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">enum</span> <span class="nc">S</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Atom</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="cm">/* … */</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Cons</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="cm">/* … */</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_10_5" className="constructor">{`S`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`::`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span>::<span class="n">S</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">Atom</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_11_4" className="constructor">{`Atom`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`i`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ =>\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Writes formatted data into a buffer.</p>
<p>This macro accepts a 'writer', a format string, and a list of arguments. Arguments will be<br>
formatted according to the specified format string and the result will be passed to the writer.<br>
The writer may be any value with a <code>write_fmt</code> method; generally this comes from an<br>
implementation of either the [<code>fmt::Write</code>] or the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/trait.Write.html"><code>io::Write</code></a> trait. The macro<br>
returns whatever the <code>write_fmt</code> method returns; commonly a [<code>fmt::Result</code>], or an<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/type.Result.html"><code>io::Result</code></a>.</p>
<p>See <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/fmt/index.html"><code>std::fmt</code></a> for more information on the format string syntax.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;test&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;formatted {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;testformatted arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>A module can import both <code>std::fmt::Write</code> and <code>std::io::Write</code> and call <code>write!</code> on objects<br>
implementing either, as objects do not typically implement both. However, the module must<br>
avoid conflict between the trait names, such as by importing them as <code>_</code> or otherwise renaming<br>
them:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Box</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="k">dyn</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">error</span>::<span class="n">Error</span><span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;{} {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;abc&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">123</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses fmt::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;s = {:?}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses io::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;s = </span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">abc 123</span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>If you also need the trait names themselves, such as to implement one or both on your types,<br>
import the containing module and then name them with a prefix:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">Example</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">impl</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Example</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">write_str</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_s</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">         </span><span class="fm">unimplemented!</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note: This macro can be used in <code>no_std</code> setups as well.<br>
In a <code>no_std</code> setup you are responsible for the implementation details of the components.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">m</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Example</span><span class="p">{};</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`write`}</span></Tooltip><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Writes formatted data into a buffer.</p>
<p>This macro accepts a 'writer', a format string, and a list of arguments. Arguments will be<br>
formatted according to the specified format string and the result will be passed to the writer.<br>
The writer may be any value with a <code>write_fmt</code> method; generally this comes from an<br>
implementation of either the [<code>fmt::Write</code>] or the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/trait.Write.html"><code>io::Write</code></a> trait. The macro<br>
returns whatever the <code>write_fmt</code> method returns; commonly a [<code>fmt::Result</code>], or an<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/type.Result.html"><code>io::Result</code></a>.</p>
<p>See <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/fmt/index.html"><code>std::fmt</code></a> for more information on the format string syntax.</p>

<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">

implementing either, as objects do not typically implement both. However, the module must<br>
avoid conflict between the trait names, such as by importing them as <code>_</code> or otherwise renaming<br>

<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Box</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="k">dyn</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">error</span>::<span class="n">Error</span><span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;{} {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;abc&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">123</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses fmt::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;s = {:?}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses io::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;s = </span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">abc 123</span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>If you also need the trait names themselves, such as to implement one or both on your types,<br>
import the containing module and then name them with a prefix:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">Example</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">impl</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Example</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">write_str</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_s</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">

\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Writes formatted data into a buffer.</p>
<p>This macro accepts a 'writer', a format string, and a list of arguments. Arguments will be<br>
formatted according to the specified format string and the result will be passed to the writer.<br>
The writer may be any value with a <code>write_fmt</code> method; generally this comes from an<br>
implementation of either the [<code>fmt::Write</code>] or the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/trait.Write.html"><code>io::Write</code></a> trait. The macro<br>
returns whatever the <code>write_fmt</code> method returns; commonly a [<code>fmt::Result</code>], or an<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/type.Result.html"><code>io::Result</code></a>.</p>
<p>See <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/fmt/index.html"><code>std::fmt</code></a> for more information on the format string syntax.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;test&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;formatted {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;testformatted arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>A module can import both <code>std::fmt::Write</code> and <code>std::io::Write</code> and call <code>write!</code> on objects<br>
implementing either, as objects do not typically implement both. However, the module must<br>
avoid conflict between the trait names, such as by importing them as <code>_</code> or otherwise renaming<br>
them:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Box</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="k">dyn</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">error</span>::<span class="n">Error</span><span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;{} {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;abc&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">123</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses fmt::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;s = {:?}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses io::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;s = </span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">abc 123</span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>If you also need the trait names themselves, such as to implement one or both on your types,<br>
import the containing module and then name them with a prefix:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">Example</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">impl</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Example</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">write_str</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_s</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">         </span><span class="fm">unimplemented!</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note: This macro can be used in <code>no_std</code> setups as well.<br>
In a <code>no_std</code> setup you are responsible for the implementation details of the components.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">write_str</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_s</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">         </span><span class="fm">unimplemented!</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">m</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Example</span><span class="p">{};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">m</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;Hello World&#34;</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">expect</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;Not written&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`write`}</span></Tooltip><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Writes formatted data into a buffer.</p>
<p>This macro accepts a 'writer', a format string, and a list of arguments. Arguments will be<br>
formatted according to the specified format string and the result will be passed to the writer.<br>
The writer may be any value with a <code>write_fmt</code> method; generally this comes from an<br>
implementation of either the [<code>fmt::Write</code>] or the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/trait.Write.html"><code>io::Write</code></a> trait. The macro<br>
returns whatever the <code>write_fmt</code> method returns; commonly a [<code>fmt::Result</code>], or an<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/type.Result.html"><code>io::Result</code></a>.</p>
<p>See <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/fmt/index.html"><code>std::fmt</code></a> for more information on the format string syntax.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;test&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;formatted {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;testformatted arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>A module can import both <code>std::fmt::Write</code> and <code>std::io::Write</code> and call <code>write!</code> on objects<br>
implementing either, as objects do not typically implement both. However, the module must<br>
avoid conflict between the trait names, such as by importing them as <code>_</code> or otherwise renaming<br>
them:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Box</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="k">dyn</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">error</span>::<span class="n">Error</span><span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;{} {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;abc&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">123</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses fmt::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;s = {:?}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses io::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;s = </span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">abc 123</span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>If you also need the trait names themselves, such as to implement one or both on your types,<br>
import the containing module and then name them with a prefix:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">impl</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Example</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">write_str</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_s</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note: This macro can be used in <code>no_std</code> setups as well.<br>
In a <code>no_std</code> setup you are responsible for the implementation details of the components.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">

\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`for`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ s\ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`in`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ rest\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Writes formatted data into a buffer.</p>
<p>This macro accepts a 'writer', a format string, and a list of arguments. Arguments will be<br>
formatted according to the specified format string and the result will be passed to the writer.<br>
The writer may be any value with a <code>write_fmt</code> method; generally this comes from an<br>
implementation of either the [<code>fmt::Write</code>] or the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/trait.Write.html"><code>io::Write</code></a> trait. The macro<br>
returns whatever the <code>write_fmt</code> method returns; commonly a [<code>fmt::Result</code>], or an<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/type.Result.html"><code>io::Result</code></a>.</p>
<p>See <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/fmt/index.html"><code>std::fmt</code></a> for more information on the format string syntax.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;test&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;formatted {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;testformatted arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>A module can import both <code>std::fmt::Write</code> and <code>std::io::Write</code> and call <code>write!</code> on objects<br>
implementing either, as objects do not typically implement both. However, the module must<br>
avoid conflict between the trait names, such as by importing them as <code>_</code> or otherwise renaming<br>
them:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Box</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="k">dyn</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">error</span>::<span class="n">Error</span><span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;{} {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;abc&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">123</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses fmt::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;s = {:?}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses io::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;s = </span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">abc 123</span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><p>If you also need the trait names themselves, such as to implement one or both on your types,<br>
import the containing module and then name them with a prefix:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`write`}</span></Tooltip><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Writes formatted data into a buffer.</p>
<p>This macro accepts a 'writer', a format string, and a list of arguments. Arguments will be<br>
formatted according to the specified format string and the result will be passed to the writer.<br>
The writer may be any value with a <code>write_fmt</code> method; generally this comes from an<br>
implementation of either the [<code>fmt::Write</code>] or the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/trait.Write.html"><code>io::Write</code></a> trait. The macro<br>
returns whatever the <code>write_fmt</code> method returns; commonly a [<code>fmt::Result</code>], or an<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/type.Result.html"><code>io::Result</code></a>.</p>
<p>See <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/fmt/index.html"><code>std::fmt</code></a> for more information on the format string syntax.</p>

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;test&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">

implementing either, as objects do not typically implement both. However, the module must<br>
avoid conflict between the trait names, such as by importing them as <code>_</code> or otherwise renaming<br>
them:</p>

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`!`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`f`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="string">{`"\ {}"`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ s`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`?
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Writes formatted data into a buffer.</p>
<p>This macro accepts a 'writer', a format string, and a list of arguments. Arguments will be<br>
formatted according to the specified format string and the result will be passed to the writer.<br>
The writer may be any value with a <code>write_fmt</code> method; generally this comes from an<br>
implementation of either the [<code>fmt::Write</code>] or the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/trait.Write.html"><code>io::Write</code></a> trait. The macro<br>
returns whatever the <code>write_fmt</code> method returns; commonly a [<code>fmt::Result</code>], or an<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/type.Result.html"><code>io::Result</code></a>.</p>
<p>See <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/fmt/index.html"><code>std::fmt</code></a> for more information on the format string syntax.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;test&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;formatted {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;testformatted arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>A module can import both <code>std::fmt::Write</code> and <code>std::io::Write</code> and call <code>write!</code> on objects<br>
implementing either, as objects do not typically implement both. However, the module must<br>
avoid conflict between the trait names, such as by importing them as <code>_</code> or otherwise renaming<br>
them:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Box</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="k">dyn</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">error</span>::<span class="n">Error</span><span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;{} {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;abc&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">123</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses fmt::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;s = {:?}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">?</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// uses io::Write::write_fmt
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sa">b</span><span class="s">&#34;s = </span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">abc 123</span><span class="se">\\&#34;</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>If you also need the trait names themselves, such as to implement one or both on your types,<br>
import the containing module and then name them with a prefix:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">Example</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">impl</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Example</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">write_str</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_s</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">         </span><span class="fm">unimplemented!</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note: This macro can be used in <code>no_std</code> setups as well.<br>
In a <code>no_std</code> setup you are responsible for the implementation details of the components.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">         </span><span class="fm">unimplemented!</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">m</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Example</span><span class="p">{};</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`write`}</span></Tooltip><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Writes formatted data into a buffer.</p>
<p>This macro accepts a 'writer', a format string, and a list of arguments. Arguments will be<br>
formatted according to the specified format string and the result will be passed to the writer.<br>
The writer may be any value with a <code>write_fmt</code> method; generally this comes from an<br>
implementation of either the [<code>fmt::Write</code>] or the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/trait.Write.html"><code>io::Write</code></a> trait. The macro<br>
returns whatever the <code>write_fmt</code> method returns; commonly a [<code>fmt::Result</code>], or an<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/io/type.Result.html"><code>io::Result</code></a>.</p>
<p>See <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/std/fmt/index.html"><code>std::fmt</code></a> for more information on the format string syntax.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">

implementing either, as objects do not typically implement both. However, the module must<br>
avoid conflict between the trait names, such as by importing them as <code>_</code> or otherwise renaming<br>

</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note: This macro can be used in <code>no_std</code> setups as well.<br>
In a <code>no_std</code> setup you are responsible for the implementation details of the components.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nc">Example</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">impl</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Write</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Example</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">write_str</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_s</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">         </span><span class="fm">unimplemented!</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">m</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Example</span><span class="p">{};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">write!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">m</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;Hello World&#34;</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">expect</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;Not written&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`!`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`f`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="string">{`")"`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

`}</span><span className="attribute">{`#`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`[`}</span><span className="attribute">{`derive`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">fmt</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kr">macro</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Debug</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Derive macro generating an impl of the trait <code>Debug</code>.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="constructor">{`Debug`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="attribute">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">clone</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kr">macro</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Clone</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Derive macro generating an impl of the trait <code>Clone</code>.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="constructor">{`Clone`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="attribute">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">marker</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kr">macro</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Copy</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Derive macro generating an impl of the trait <code>Copy</code>.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="constructor">{`Copy`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="attribute">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">cmp</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kr">macro</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">PartialEq</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
