</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;y&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;e&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">

<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">y</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;y̆&#34;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.method">{`chars`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">P</span>: <span class="nb">FnMut</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="bp">Self</span>::<span class="n">Item</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="kt">bool</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p><code>Self</code> = <code>Chars&lt;'_&gt;</code>, <code>P</code> = <code>impl FnMut(&amp;char) -&gt; …</code></p>
<hr>
<p>Creates an iterator which uses a closure to determine if an element<br>
should be yielded.</p>
<p>Given an element the closure must return <code>true</code> or <code>false</code>. The returned<br>
iterator will yield only the elements for which the closure returns<br>
<code>true</code>.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<p>Basic usage:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="k">i32</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">into_iter</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">filter</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">is_positive</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Because the closure passed to <code>filter()</code> takes a reference, and many<br>
iterators iterate over references, this leads to a possibly confusing<br>
situation, where the type of the closure is a double reference:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">filter</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">**</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// needs two *s!
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>It's common to instead use destructuring on the argument to strip away one:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">filter</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|&amp;</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// both &amp; and *
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>or both:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">filter</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|&amp;&amp;</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// two &amp;s
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>of these layers.</p>
<p>Note that <code>iter.filter(f).next()</code> is equivalent to <code>iter.find(f)</code>.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="property">{`filter`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`|it|\ !it`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`.`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">methods</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">const</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">is_ascii_whitespace</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="kt">bool</span>
</span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Checks if the value is an ASCII whitespace character:<br>
U+0020 SPACE, U+0009 HORIZONTAL TAB, U+000A LINE FEED,<br>
U+000C FORM FEED, or U+000D CARRIAGE RETURN.</p>
<p>Rust uses the WhatWG Infra Standard's <a href="https://infra.spec.whatwg.org/#ascii-whitespace">definition of ASCII<br>
whitespace</a>. There are several other definitions in<br>
wide use. For instance, <a href="https://pubs.opengroup.org/onlinepubs/9699919799/basedefs/V1_chap07.html#tag_07_03_01">the POSIX locale</a> includes<br>
U+000B VERTICAL TAB as well as all the above characters,<br>
but—from the very same specification—<a href="https://pubs.opengroup.org/onlinepubs/9699919799/utilities/V3_chap02.html#tag_18_06_05">the default rule for<br>
&quot;field splitting&quot; in the Bourne shell</a> considers <em>only</em><br>
SPACE, HORIZONTAL TAB, and LINE FEED as whitespace.</p>
<p>If you are writing a program that will process an existing<br>
file format, check what that format's definition of whitespace is<br>
before using this function.</p>

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">g</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;g&#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">zero</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;0&#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">percent</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;%&#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">space</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39; &#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">lf</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\n&#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">esc</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\x1b&#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="n">uppercase_a</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">is_ascii_whitespace</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="n">uppercase_g</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">is_ascii_whitespace</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">is_ascii_whitespace</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="n">g</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">is_ascii_whitespace</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="n">zero</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">is_ascii_whitespace</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="n">esc</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">is_ascii_whitespace</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="property">{`is_ascii_whitespace`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`.`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">iter</span>::<span class="n">traits</span>::<span class="n">iterator</span>::<span class="nb">Iterator</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">trait</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Iterator</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">map</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">B</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">F</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">f</span>: <span class="nc">F</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">Map</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="bp">Self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">F</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">where</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="bp">Self</span>: <span class="nb">Sized</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">F</span>: <span class="nb">FnMut</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="bp">Self</span>::<span class="n">Item</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">B</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p><code>Self</code> = <code>Filter&lt;Chars&lt;'_&gt;, impl FnMut(…) -&gt; …&gt;</code>, <code>B</code> = <code>Token</code>, <code>F</code> = <code>impl FnMut(char) -&gt; …</code></p>
<hr>
<p>Takes a closure and creates an iterator which calls that closure on each<br>
element.</p>
<p><code>map()</code> transforms one iterator into another, by means of its argument:<br>
something that implements <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/ops/function/trait.FnMut.html"><code>FnMut</code></a>. It produces a new iterator which<br>
calls this closure on each element of the original iterator.</p>
<p>If you are good at thinking in types, you can think of <code>map()</code> like this:<br>
If you have an iterator that gives you elements of some type <code>A</code>, and<br>
you want an iterator of some other type <code>B</code>, you can use <code>map()</code>,<br>
passing a closure that takes an <code>A</code> and returns a <code>B</code>.</p>
<p><code>map()</code> is conceptually similar to a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/iter/book/ch03-05-control-flow.html#looping-through-a-collection-with-for"><code>for</code></a> loop. However, as <code>map()</code> is<br>
lazy, it is best used when you're already working with other iterators.<br>
If you're doing some sort of looping for a side effect, it's considered<br>
more idiomatic to use <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/iter/book/ch03-05-control-flow.html#looping-through-a-collection-with-for"><code>for</code></a> than <code>map()</code>.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<p>Basic usage:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">map</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>If you're doing some sort of side effect, prefer <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/iter/book/ch03-05-control-flow.html#looping-through-a-collection-with-for"><code>for</code></a> to <code>map()</code>:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// don&#39;t do this:
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">map</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{x}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// it won&#39;t even execute, as it is lazy. Rust will warn you about this.
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Instead, use a for-loop:
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{x}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="property">{`map`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`|c|\ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`match`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ c\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="string">{`'0'`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`..=`}</span><span className="string">{`'9'`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ |\ `}</span><span className="string">{`'a'`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`..=`}</span><span className="string">{`'z'`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ |\ `}</span><span className="string">{`'A'`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`..=`}</span><span className="string">{`'Z'`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ =>\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Atom</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="cm">/* … */</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Op</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="cm">/* … */</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Eof</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_31_5" className="constructor">{`Token`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`::`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span>::<span class="n">Token</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_32_4" className="constructor">{`Atom`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`c`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ _\ =>\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">enum</span> <span class="nc">Token</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Atom</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="cm">/* … */</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w">

\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`.`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">iter</span>::<span class="n">traits</span>::<span class="n">iterator</span>::<span class="nb">Iterator</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">trait</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Iterator</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">collect</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">B</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">B</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">where</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">B</span>: <span class="nc">FromIterator</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="bp">Self</span>::<span class="n">Item</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="bp">Self</span>: <span class="nb">Sized</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p><code>Self</code> = <code>Map&lt;Filter&lt;Chars&lt;'_&gt;, …&gt;, …&gt;</code>, <code>B</code> = <code>Vec&lt;Token&gt;</code></p>
<hr>
<p>Transforms an iterator into a collection.</p>
<p><code>collect()</code> can take anything iterable, and turn it into a relevant<br>
collection. This is one of the more powerful methods in the standard<br>
library, used in a variety of contexts.</p>
<p>The most basic pattern in which <code>collect()</code> is used is to turn one<br>
collection into another. You take a collection, call [<code>iter</code>] on it,<br>
do a bunch of transformations, and then <code>collect()</code> at the end.</p>
<p><code>collect()</code> can also create instances of types that are not typical<br>
collections. For example, a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/iter/std/string/struct.String.html"><code>String</code></a> can be built from [<code>char</code>]s,<br>
and an iterator of <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/result/enum.Result.html"><code>Result&lt;T, E&gt;</code></a> items can be collected<br>
into <code>Result&lt;Collection&lt;T&gt;, E&gt;</code>. See the examples below for more.</p>
<p>Because <code>collect()</code> is so general, it can cause problems with type<br>
inference. As such, <code>collect()</code> is one of the few times you'll see<br>
the syntax affectionately known as the 'turbofish': <code>::&lt;&gt;</code>. This<br>
helps the inference algorithm understand specifically which collection<br>
you're trying to collect into.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<p>Basic usage:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">doubled</span>: <span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">i32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">                         </span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">map</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">                         </span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">collect</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">doubled</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note that we needed the <code>: Vec&lt;i32&gt;</code> on the left-hand side. This is because<br>
we could collect into, for example, a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/iter/std/collections/struct.VecDeque.html"><code>VecDeque&lt;T&gt;</code></a> instead:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">collections</span>::<span class="n">VecDeque</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">doubled</span>: <span class="nc">VecDeque</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">i32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">map</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">collect</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">doubled</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">doubled</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">doubled</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Using the 'turbofish' instead of annotating <code>doubled</code>:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">doubled</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">map</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">collect</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">i32</span><span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">doubled</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Because <code>collect()</code> only cares about what you're collecting into, you can<br>
still use a partial type hint, <code>_</code>, with the turbofish:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">doubled</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">iter</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">map</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">collect</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">_</span><span class="o">&gt;&gt;</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">doubled</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Using <code>collect()</code> to make a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/iter/std/string/struct.String.html"><code>String</code></a>:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;g&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;d&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;k&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;k&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;n&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">hello</span>: <span class="nb">String</span> <span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">into_iter</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">map</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">map</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="o">|</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">+</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">as</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">collect</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;hello&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">hello</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>If you have a list of <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/result/enum.Result.html"><code>Result&lt;T, E&gt;</code></a>s, you can use <code>collect()</code> to<br>
see if any of them failed:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">results</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Err</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;nope&#34;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Err</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;bad&#34;</span><span class="p">)];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">result</span>: <span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">_</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">results</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">into_iter</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">collect</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// gives us the first error
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Err</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;nope&#34;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">result</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">results</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">)];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">result</span>: <span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">_</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">results</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">into_iter</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">collect</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// gives us the list of answers
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">]),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">result</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="property">{`collect`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`::`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`<`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">vec</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">struct</span> <span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">A</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Global</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">where</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">A</span>: <span class="nc">Allocator</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">buf</span>: <span class="nc">RawVec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">A</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">len</span>: <span class="kt">usize</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>A contiguous growable array type, written as <code>Vec&lt;T&gt;</code>, short for 'vector'.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">pop</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">7</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">7</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">extend</span><span class="p">([</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">for</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">in</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{x}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">7</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>The <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/macros/macro.vec.html"><code>vec</code></a> macro is provided for convenient initialization:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec1</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec1</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec2</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">([</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>It can also initialize each element of a <code>Vec&lt;T&gt;</code> with a given value.<br>
This may be more efficient than performing allocation and initialization<br>
in separate steps, especially when initializing a vector of zeros:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// The following is equivalent, but potentially slower:
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">with_capacity</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">resize</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>For more information, see<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/vec/struct.Vec.html#capacity-and-reallocation">Capacity and Reallocation</a>.</p>
<p>Use a <code>Vec&lt;T&gt;</code> as an efficient stack:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">stack</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">stack</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">stack</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">stack</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">push</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">while</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">top</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">stack</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">pop</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="c1">// Prints 3, 2, 1
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{top}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><h1 id="indexing">Indexing</h1>
<p>The <code>Vec</code> type allows access to values by index, because it implements the<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/ops/index/trait.Index.html"><code>Index</code></a> trait. An example will be more explicit:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// it will display &#39;2&#39;
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>However be careful: if you try to access an index which isn't in the <code>Vec</code>,<br>
your software will panic! You cannot do this:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">4</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="si">{}</span><span class="s">&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">6</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// it will panic!
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Use [<code>get</code>] and [<code>get_mut</code>] if you want to check whether the index is in<br>
the <code>Vec</code>.</p>
<h1 id="slicing">Slicing</h1>
<p>A <code>Vec</code> can be mutable. On the other hand, slices are read-only objects.<br>
To get a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/slice/index.html">slice</a>, use <a href="%60&amp;%60"><code>&amp;</code></a>. Example:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">read_slice</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">slice</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="kt">usize</span><span class="p">])</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="c1">// ...
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">read_slice</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// ... and that&#39;s all!
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// you can also do it like this:
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">u</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="kt">usize</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// or like this:
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">u</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="n">_</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>In Rust, it's more common to pass slices as arguments rather than vectors<br>
when you just want to provide read access. The same goes for [<code>String</code>] and<br>
[<code>&amp;str</code>].</p>
<h1 id="capacity-and-reallocation">Capacity and reallocation</h1>
<p>The capacity of a vector is the amount of space allocated for any future<br>
elements that will be added onto the vector. This is not to be confused with<br>
the <em>length</em> of a vector, which specifies the number of actual elements<br>
within the vector. If a vector's length exceeds its capacity, its capacity<br>
will automatically be increased, but its elements will have to be<br>
reallocated.</p>
<p>For example, a vector with capacity 10 and length 0 would be an empty vector<br>
with space for 10 more elements. Pushing 10 or fewer elements onto the<br>
vector will not change its capacity or cause reallocation to occur. However,<br>
if the vector's length is increased to 11, it will have to reallocate, which<br>
can be slow. For this reason, it is recommended to use <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/vec/struct.Vec.html#method.with_capacity"><code>Vec::with_capacity</code></a><br>
whenever possible to specify how big the vector is expected to get.</p>
<h1 id="guarantees">Guarantees</h1>
<p>Due to its incredibly fundamental nature, <code>Vec</code> makes a lot of guarantees<br>
about its design. This ensures that it's as low-overhead as possible in<br>
the general case, and can be correctly manipulated in primitive ways<br>
by unsafe code. Note that these guarantees refer to an unqualified <code>Vec&lt;T&gt;</code>.<br>
If additional type parameters are added (e.g., to support custom allocators),<br>
overriding their defaults may change the behavior.</p>
<p>Most fundamentally, <code>Vec</code> is and always will be a (pointer, capacity, length)<br>
triplet. No more, no less. The order of these fields is completely<br>
unspecified, and you should use the appropriate methods to modify these.<br>
The pointer will never be null, so this type is null-pointer-optimized.</p>
<p>However, the pointer might not actually point to allocated memory. In particular,<br>
if you construct a <code>Vec</code> with capacity 0 via <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/vec/struct.Vec.html#method.new"><code>Vec::new</code></a>, <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/macros/macro.vec.html"><code>vec![]</code></a>,<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/vec/struct.Vec.html#method.with_capacity"><code>Vec::with_capacity(0)</code></a>, or by calling [<code>shrink_to_fit</code>]<br>
on an empty Vec, it will not allocate memory. Similarly, if you store zero-sized<br>
types inside a <code>Vec</code>, it will not allocate space for them. <em>Note that in this case<br>
the <code>Vec</code> might not report a [<code>capacity</code>] of 0</em>. <code>Vec</code> will allocate if and only<br>
if <code><br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/mem/fn.size_of.html">size_of::&lt;T&gt;</a>() * <a href="">capacity</a> &gt; 0</code>. In general, <code>Vec</code>'s allocation<br>
details are very subtle --- if you intend to allocate memory using a <code>Vec</code><br>
and use it for something else (either to pass to unsafe code, or to build your<br>
own memory-backed collection), be sure to deallocate this memory by using<br>
<code>from_raw_parts</code> to recover the <code>Vec</code> and then dropping it.</p>
<p>If a <code>Vec</code> <em>has</em> allocated memory, then the memory it points to is on the heap<br>
(as defined by the allocator Rust is configured to use by default), and its<br>
pointer points to [<code>len</code>] initialized, contiguous elements in order (what<br>
you would see if you coerced it to a slice), followed by <code><br>
[capacity] - [len]</code><br>
logically uninitialized, contiguous elements.</p>
<p>A vector containing the elements <code>'a'</code> and <code>'b'</code> with capacity 4 can be<br>
visualized as below. The top part is the <code>Vec</code> struct, it contains a<br>
pointer to the head of the allocation in the heap, length and capacity.<br>
The bottom part is the allocation on the heap, a contiguous memory block.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl">            ptr      len  capacity
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">       +--------+--------+--------+
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">       | 0x0123 |      2 |      4 |
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">       +--------+--------+--------+
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">            |
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">            v
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">Heap   +--------+--------+--------+--------+
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">       |    &#39;a&#39; |    &#39;b&#39; | uninit | uninit |
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">       +--------+--------+--------+--------+
</span></span></code></pre><ul>
<li><strong>uninit</strong> represents memory that is not initialized, see [<code>MaybeUninit</code>].</li>
<li>Note: the ABI is not stable and <code>Vec</code> makes no guarantees about its memory<br>
layout (including the order of fields).</li>
</ul>
<p><code>Vec</code> will never perform a &quot;small optimization&quot; where elements are actually<br>
stored on the stack for two reasons:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It would make it more difficult for unsafe code to correctly manipulate<br>
a <code>Vec</code>. The contents of a <code>Vec</code> wouldn't have a stable address if it were<br>
only moved, and it would be more difficult to determine if a <code>Vec</code> had<br>
actually allocated memory.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It would penalize the general case, incurring an additional branch<br>
on every access.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><code>Vec</code> will never automatically shrink itself, even if completely empty. This<br>
ensures no unnecessary allocations or deallocations occur. Emptying a <code>Vec</code><br>
and then filling it back up to the same [<code>len</code>] should incur no calls to<br>
the allocator. If you wish to free up unused memory, use<br>
[<code>shrink_to_fit</code>] or [<code>shrink_to</code>].</p>
<p>[<code>push</code>] and [<code>insert</code>] will never (re)allocate if the reported capacity is<br>
sufficient. [<code>push</code>] and [<code>insert</code>] <em>will</em> (re)allocate if<br>
<code><br>
[len] == [capacity]</code>. That is, the reported capacity is completely<br>
accurate, and can be relied on. It can even be used to manually free the memory<br>
allocated by a <code>Vec</code> if desired. Bulk insertion methods <em>may</em> reallocate, even<br>
when not necessary.</p>
<p><code>Vec</code> does not guarantee any particular growth strategy when reallocating<br>
when full, nor when [<code>reserve</code>] is called. The current strategy is basic<br>
and it may prove desirable to use a non-constant growth factor. Whatever<br>
strategy is used will of course guarantee <em>O</em>(1) amortized [<code>push</code>].</p>
<p>It is guaranteed, in order to respect the intentions of the programmer, that<br>
all of <code>vec![e_1, e_2, ..., e_n]</code>, <code>vec![x; n]</code>, and [<code>Vec::with_capacity(n)</code>] produce a <code>Vec</code><br>
that requests an allocation of the exact size needed for precisely <code>n</code> elements from the allocator,<br>
and no other size (such as, for example: a size rounded up to the nearest power of 2).<br>
The allocator will return an allocation that is at least as large as requested, but it may be larger.</p>
<p>It is guaranteed that the [<code>Vec::capacity</code>] method returns a value that is at least the requested capacity<br>
and not more than the allocated capacity.</p>
<p>The method <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/vec/struct.Vec.html#method.shrink_to_fit"><code>Vec::shrink_to_fit</code></a> will attempt to discard excess capacity an allocator has given to a <code>Vec</code>.<br>
If <code><br>
[len] == [capacity]</code>, then a <code>Vec&lt;T&gt;</code> can be converted<br>
to and from a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/boxed/struct.Box.html"><code>Box&lt;[T]&gt;</code></a> without reallocating or moving the elements.<br>
<code>Vec</code> exploits this fact as much as reasonable when implementing common conversions<br>
such as [<code>into_boxed_slice</code>].</p>
<p><code>Vec</code> will not specifically overwrite any data that is removed from it,<br>
but also won't specifically preserve it. Its uninitialized memory is<br>
scratch space that it may use however it wants. It will generally just do<br>
whatever is most efficient or otherwise easy to implement. Do not rely on<br>
removed data to be erased for security purposes. Even if you drop a <code>Vec</code>, its<br>
buffer may simply be reused by another allocation. Even if you zero a <code>Vec</code>'s memory<br>
first, that might not actually happen because the optimizer does not consider<br>
this a side-effect that must be preserved. There is one case which we will<br>
not break, however: using <code>unsafe</code> code to write to the excess capacity,<br>
and then increasing the length to match, is always valid.</p>
<p>Currently, <code>Vec</code> does not guarantee the order in which elements are dropped.<br>
The order has changed in the past and may change again.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type">{`Vec`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`<`}</span><span className="type">{`_`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`>`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`>`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`;`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

<p>Removes the last element from a vector and returns it, or <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/option/enum.Option.html#variant.None"><code>None</code></a> if it<br>
is empty.</p>
<p>If you'd like to pop the first element, consider using<br>
[<code>VecDeque::pop_front</code>] instead.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><h1 id="time-complexity">Time complexity</h1>
<p>Takes <em>O</em>(1) time.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="property">{`pop`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`.`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">option</span>::<span class="nb">Option</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">impl</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">const</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">unwrap_or</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">default</span>: <span class="nc">T</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">T</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">where</span><span class="w">
