</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p><code>T</code> = <code>Token</code></p>
<hr>
<p>Returns the contained <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/option/enum.Option.html#variant.Some"><code>Some</code></a> value or a provided default.</p>
<p>Arguments passed to <code>unwrap_or</code> are eagerly evaluated; if you are passing<br>
the result of a function call, it is recommended to use [<code>unwrap_or_else</code>],<br>
which is lazily evaluated.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;car&#34;</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">unwrap_or</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;bike&#34;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;car&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">unwrap_or</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;bike&#34;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;bike&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="property">{`unwrap_or`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">

<p><code>T</code> = <code>Token</code></p>
<hr>
<p>Returns the last element of the slice, or <code>None</code> if it is empty.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">10</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">40</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">30</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="mi">30</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">last</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="kt">i32</span><span class="p">]</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="p">[];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">w</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">last</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="property">{`last`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`.`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">option</span>::<span class="nb">Option</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">impl</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;&amp;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">where</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">T</span>: <span class="nb">Copy</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p><code>T</code> = <code>Token</code></p>
<hr>
<p>Maps an <code>Option&lt;&amp;T&gt;</code> to an <code>Option&lt;T&gt;</code> by copying the contents of the<br>
option.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">12</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">opt_x</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="property">{`copied`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`.`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">option</span>::<span class="nb">Option</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">impl</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">const</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">unwrap_or</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">default</span>: <span class="nc">T</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">T</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">where</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">T</span>: <span class="nc">Destruct</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p><code>T</code> = <code>Token</code></p>
<hr>
<p>Returns the contained <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/option/enum.Option.html#variant.Some"><code>Some</code></a> value or a provided default.</p>
<p>Arguments passed to <code>unwrap_or</code> are eagerly evaluated; if you are passing<br>
the result of a function call, it is recommended to use [<code>unwrap_or_else</code>],<br>
which is lazily evaluated.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;car&#34;</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">unwrap_or</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;bike&#34;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;car&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">unwrap_or</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;bike&#34;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;bike&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.method">{`unwrap_or`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">enum</span> <span class="nc">Token</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">Atom</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="cm">/* … */</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">Eof</span><span class="w">

\ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

`}</span><span className="keyword">{`fn`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">expr</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">input</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">S</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_64_3" className="function">{`expr`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">input</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span>
</span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>size = 16 (0x10), align = 0x8, no Drop</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_64_8" className="variable.parameter">{`input`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`:`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="operator">{`&`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">str</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>String slices.</p>
<p><em><a href="crate::str">See also the <code>std::str</code> module</a>.</em></p>
<p>The <code>str</code> type, also called a 'string slice', is the most primitive string<br>
type. It is usually seen in its borrowed form, <code>&amp;str</code>. It is also the type<br>
of string literals, <code>&amp;'static str</code>.</p>
<h1 id="basic-usage">Basic Usage</h1>
<p>String literals are string slices:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">hello_world</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;Hello, World!&#34;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Here we have declared a string slice initialized with a string literal.<br>
String literals have a static lifetime, which means the string <code>hello_world</code><br>
is guaranteed to be valid for the duration of the entire program.<br>
We can explicitly specify <code>hello_world</code>'s lifetime as well:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">hello_world</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="nb">&#39;static</span> <span class="kt">str</span> <span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;Hello, world!&#34;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><h1 id="representation">Representation</h1>
<p>A <code>&amp;str</code> is made up of two components: a pointer to some bytes, and a<br>
length. You can look at these with the [<code>as_ptr</code>] and [<code>len</code>] methods:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">slice</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">story</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;Once upon a time...&#34;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">ptr</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">story</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">as_ptr</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">len</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">story</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// story has nineteen bytes
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">19</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// We can re-build a str out of ptr and len. This is all unsafe because
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// we are responsible for making sure the two components are valid:
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">unsafe</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="c1">// First, we build a &amp;[u8]...
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">slice</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">slice</span>::<span class="n">from_raw_parts</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">ptr</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="c1">// ... and then convert that slice into a string slice
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kt">str</span>::<span class="n">from_utf8</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">slice</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">story</span><span class="p">));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note: This example shows the internals of <code>&amp;str</code>. <code>unsafe</code> should not be<br>
used to get a string slice under normal circumstances. Use <code>as_str</code><br>
instead.</p>
<h1 id="invariant">Invariant</h1>
<p>Rust libraries may assume that string slices are always valid UTF-8.</p>
<p>Constructing a non-UTF-8 string slice is not immediate undefined behavior, but any function<br>
called on a string slice may assume that it is valid UTF-8, which means that a non-UTF-8 string<br>
slice can lead to undefined behavior down the road.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type.builtin">{`str`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ ->\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">

\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">assert_eq</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Asserts that two expressions are equal to each other (using <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/cmp/trait.PartialEq.html"><code>PartialEq</code></a>).</p>
<p>Assertions are always checked in both debug and release builds, and cannot<br>
be disabled. See [<code>debug_assert_eq!</code>] for assertions that are disabled in<br>
release builds by default.</p>
<p>On panic, this macro will print the values of the expressions with their<br>
debug representations.</p>
<p>Like <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/macros/builtin/macro.assert.html"><code>assert</code></a>, this macro has a second form, where a custom<br>
panic message can be provided.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">+</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`assert_eq`}</span></Tooltip><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">assert_eq</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Asserts that two expressions are equal to each other (using <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/cmp/trait.PartialEq.html"><code>PartialEq</code></a>).</p>
<p>Assertions are always checked in both debug and release builds, and cannot<br>
be disabled. See [<code>debug_assert_eq!</code>] for assertions that are disabled in<br>

debug representations.</p>
<p>Like <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/macros/builtin/macro.assert.html"><code>assert</code></a>, this macro has a second form, where a custom<br>
panic message can be provided.</p>

</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">enum</span> <span class="nc">S</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_12_4" className="constructor">{`Cons`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`op`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #2
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Creates a [<code>Vec</code>] containing the arguments.</p>
<p><code>vec!</code> allows <code>Vec</code>s to be defined with the same syntax as array expressions.<br>
There are two forms of this macro:</p>
<ul>
<li>Create a [<code>Vec</code>] containing a given list of elements:</li>
</ul>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><ul>
<li>Create a [<code>Vec</code>] from a given element and size:</li>
</ul>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note that unlike array expressions this syntax supports all elements<br>
which implement <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/clone/trait.Clone.html"><code>Clone</code></a> and the number of elements doesn't have to be<br>
a constant.</p>
<p>This will use <code>clone</code> to duplicate an expression, so one should be careful<br>
using this with types having a nonstandard <code>Clone</code> implementation. For<br>
example, <code>vec![Rc::new(1); 5]</code> will create a vector of five references<br>
to the same boxed integer value, not five references pointing to independently<br>
boxed integers.</p>
<p>Also, note that <code>vec![expr; 0]</code> is allowed, and produces an empty vector.<br>
This will still evaluate <code>expr</code>, however, and immediately drop the resulting value, so<br>
be mindful of side effects.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`vec`}</span></Tooltip><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #2
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Creates a [<code>Vec</code>] containing the arguments.</p>
<p><code>vec!</code> allows <code>Vec</code>s to be defined with the same syntax as array expressions.<br>
There are two forms of this macro:</p>
<ul>
<li>Create a [<code>Vec</code>] containing a given list of elements:</li>
</ul>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><ul>
<li>Create a [<code>Vec</code>] from a given element and size:</li>
</ul>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note that unlike array expressions this syntax supports all elements<br>
which implement <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/clone/trait.Clone.html"><code>Clone</code></a> and the number of elements doesn't have to be<br>
a constant.</p>
<p>This will use <code>clone</code> to duplicate an expression, so one should be careful<br>
using this with types having a nonstandard <code>Clone</code> implementation. For<br>
example, <code>vec![Rc::new(1); 5]</code> will create a vector of five references<br>
to the same boxed integer value, not five references pointing to independently<br>
boxed integers.</p>
<p>Also, note that <code>vec![expr; 0]</code> is allowed, and produces an empty vector.<br>
This will still evaluate <code>expr</code>, however, and immediately drop the resulting value, so<br>
be mindful of side effects.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`!`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`[`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`rhs`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`]`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">assert_eq</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Asserts that two expressions are equal to each other (using <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/cmp/trait.PartialEq.html"><code>PartialEq</code></a>).</p>
<p>Assertions are always checked in both debug and release builds, and cannot<br>
be disabled. See [<code>debug_assert_eq!</code>] for assertions that are disabled in<br>
release builds by default.</p>
<p>On panic, this macro will print the values of the expressions with their<br>
debug representations.</p>
<p>Like <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/macros/builtin/macro.assert.html"><code>assert</code></a>, this macro has a second form, where a custom<br>
panic message can be provided.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>

</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">Cons</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">S</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_12_4" className="function">{`Cons`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`op`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #2
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Creates a [<code>Vec</code>] containing the arguments.</p>
<p><code>vec!</code> allows <code>Vec</code>s to be defined with the same syntax as array expressions.<br>
There are two forms of this macro:</p>
<ul>
<li>Create a [<code>Vec</code>] containing a given list of elements:</li>
</ul>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><ul>
<li>Create a [<code>Vec</code>] from a given element and size:</li>
</ul>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note that unlike array expressions this syntax supports all elements<br>
which implement <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/clone/trait.Clone.html"><code>Clone</code></a> and the number of elements doesn't have to be<br>
a constant.</p>
<p>This will use <code>clone</code> to duplicate an expression, so one should be careful<br>
using this with types having a nonstandard <code>Clone</code> implementation. For<br>
example, <code>vec![Rc::new(1); 5]</code> will create a vector of five references<br>
to the same boxed integer value, not five references pointing to independently<br>
boxed integers.</p>
<p>Also, note that <code>vec![expr; 0]</code> is allowed, and produces an empty vector.<br>
This will still evaluate <code>expr</code>, however, and immediately drop the resulting value, so<br>
be mindful of side effects.</p>

\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">assert_eq</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Asserts that two expressions are equal to each other (using <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/cmp/trait.PartialEq.html"><code>PartialEq</code></a>).</p>
<p>Assertions are always checked in both debug and release builds, and cannot<br>
be disabled. See [<code>debug_assert_eq!</code>] for assertions that are disabled in<br>
release builds by default.</p>
<p>On panic, this macro will print the values of the expressions with their<br>
debug representations.</p>
<p>Like <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/macros/builtin/macro.assert.html"><code>assert</code></a>, this macro has a second form, where a custom<br>
panic message can be provided.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">enum</span> <span class="nc">S</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">Cons</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">S</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_12_4" className="constructor">{`Cons`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`op`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #2
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Creates a [<code>Vec</code>] containing the arguments.</p>
<p><code>vec!</code> allows <code>Vec</code>s to be defined with the same syntax as array expressions.<br>
There are two forms of this macro:</p>
<ul>
<li>Create a [<code>Vec</code>] containing a given list of elements:</li>
</ul>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><ul>
<li>Create a [<code>Vec</code>] from a given element and size:</li>
</ul>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note that unlike array expressions this syntax supports all elements<br>
which implement <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/clone/trait.Clone.html"><code>Clone</code></a> and the number of elements doesn't have to be<br>
a constant.</p>
<p>This will use <code>clone</code> to duplicate an expression, so one should be careful<br>
using this with types having a nonstandard <code>Clone</code> implementation. For<br>
example, <code>vec![Rc::new(1); 5]</code> will create a vector of five references<br>
to the same boxed integer value, not five references pointing to independently<br>
boxed integers.</p>
<p>Also, note that <code>vec![expr; 0]</code> is allowed, and produces an empty vector.<br>
This will still evaluate <code>expr</code>, however, and immediately drop the resulting value, so<br>
be mindful of side effects.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`vec`}</span></Tooltip><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">vec</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #2
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Creates a [<code>Vec</code>] containing the arguments.</p>
<p><code>vec!</code> allows <code>Vec</code>s to be defined with the same syntax as array expressions.<br>
There are two forms of this macro:</p>
<ul>
<li>Create a [<code>Vec</code>] containing a given list of elements:</li>
</ul>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">],</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><ul>
<li>Create a [<code>Vec</code>] from a given element and size:</li>
</ul>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">[</span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="p">]);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Note that unlike array expressions this syntax supports all elements<br>
which implement <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/clone/trait.Clone.html"><code>Clone</code></a> and the number of elements doesn't have to be<br>
a constant.</p>
<p>This will use <code>clone</code> to duplicate an expression, so one should be careful<br>
using this with types having a nonstandard <code>Clone</code> implementation. For<br>
example, <code>vec![Rc::new(1); 5]</code> will create a vector of five references<br>
to the same boxed integer value, not five references pointing to independently<br>
boxed integers.</p>
<p>Also, note that <code>vec![expr; 0]</code> is allowed, and produces an empty vector.<br>
This will still evaluate <code>expr</code>, however, and immediately drop the resulting value, so<br>
be mindful of side effects.</p>
