</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">prefix_binding_power</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">op</span>: <span class="kt">char</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="p">((),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_132_3" className="function">{`prefix_binding_power`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">op</span>: <span class="kt">char</span>
</span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>size = 4, align = 0x4, no Drop</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_132_24" className="variable.parameter">{`op`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`:`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">char</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>A character type.</p>
<p>The <code>char</code> type represents a single character. More specifically, since<br>
'character' isn't a well-defined concept in Unicode, <code>char</code> is a '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#unicode_scalar_value">Unicode<br>
scalar value</a>'.</p>
<p>This documentation describes a number of methods and trait implementations on the<br>
<code>char</code> type. For technical reasons, there is additional, separate<br>
documentation in <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/char/index.html">the <code>std::char</code> module</a> as well.</p>
<h1 id="validity-and-layout">Validity and Layout</h1>
<p>A <code>char</code> is a '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#unicode_scalar_value">Unicode scalar value</a>', which is any '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#code_point">Unicode code point</a>'<br>
other than a <a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_code_point">surrogate code point</a>. This has a fixed numerical definition:<br>
code points are in the range 0 to 0x10FFFF, inclusive.<br>
Surrogate code points, used by UTF-16, are in the range 0xD800 to 0xDFFF.</p>
<p>No <code>char</code> may be constructed, whether as a literal or at runtime, that is not a<br>
Unicode scalar value. Violating this rule causes undefined behavior.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Each of these is a compiler error
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{D800}&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{DFFF}&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{110000}&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Panics; from_u32 returns None.
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">from_u32</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mh">0xDE01</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">unwrap</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Undefined behavior
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">unsafe</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">from_u32_unchecked</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mh">0x110000</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Unicode scalar values are also the exact set of values that may be encoded in UTF-8. Because<br>
<code>char</code> values are Unicode scalar values and functions may assume <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/primitive.str.html#invariant">incoming <code>str</code> values are<br>
valid UTF-8</a>, it is safe to store any <code>char</code> in a <code>str</code> or read<br>
any character from a <code>str</code> as a <code>char</code>.</p>
<p>The gap in valid <code>char</code> values is understood by the compiler, so in the<br>
below example the two ranges are understood to cover the whole range of<br>
possible <code>char</code> values and there is no error for a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/book/ch06-02-match.html#matches-are-exhaustive">non-exhaustive match</a>.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">c</span>: <span class="kt">char</span> <span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;a&#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">match</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">c</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\0&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">..=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{D7FF}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">false</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{E000}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">..=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{10FFFF}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">true</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>All Unicode scalar values are valid <code>char</code> values, but not all of them represent a real<br>
character. Many Unicode scalar values are not currently assigned to a character, but may be in<br>
the future (&quot;reserved&quot;); some will never be a character (&quot;noncharacters&quot;); and some may be given<br>
different meanings by different users (&quot;private use&quot;).</p>
<p><code>char</code> is guaranteed to have the same size, alignment, and function call ABI as <code>u32</code> on all<br>
platforms.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">Layout</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">Layout</span>::<span class="n">new</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Layout</span>::<span class="n">new</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><h1 id="representation">Representation</h1>
<p><code>char</code> is always four bytes in size. This is a different representation than<br>
a given character would have as part of a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/string/struct.String.html"><code>String</code></a>. For example:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;h&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;e&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;l&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;l&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;o&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// five elements times four bytes for each element
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">20</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;hello&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// five elements times one byte per element
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>As always, remember that a human intuition for 'character' might not map to<br>
Unicode's definitions. For example, despite looking similar, the 'é'<br>
character is one Unicode code point while 'é' is two Unicode code points:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;é&#34;</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+00e9: &#39;latin small letter e with acute&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{00e9}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;é&#34;</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+0065: &#39;latin small letter e&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{0065}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+0301: &#39;combining acute accent&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{0301}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>This means that the contents of the first string above <em>will</em> fit into a<br>
<code>char</code> while the contents of the second string <em>will not</em>. Trying to create<br>
a <code>char</code> literal with the contents of the second string gives an error:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl">error: character literal may only contain one codepoint: &#39;é&#39;
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">let c = &#39;é&#39;;
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">        ^^^
</span></span></code></pre><p>Another implication of the 4-byte fixed size of a <code>char</code> is that<br>
per-<code>char</code> processing can end up using a lot more memory:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;love: ❤️&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span>: <span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">collect</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">12</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of_val</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="p">]));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">32</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of_val</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="p">]));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type.builtin">{`char`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ ->\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>The 8-bit unsigned integer type.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type.builtin">{`u8`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`match`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ op\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="string">{`'+'`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ |\ `}</span><span className="string">{`'-'`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ =>\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>value of literal: <code>9 (0x9|0b1001)</code></p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="constant.builtin">{`9`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ _\ =>\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">panic</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`panic`}</span></Tooltip><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">panic</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`!`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="string">{`"bad\ op:\ {:?}"`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ op`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

`}</span><span className="keyword">{`fn`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">postfix_binding_power</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">op</span>: <span class="kt">char</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">())</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_139_3" className="function">{`postfix_binding_power`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">op</span>: <span class="kt">char</span>
</span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>size = 4, align = 0x4, no Drop</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_139_25" className="variable.parameter">{`op`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`:`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">char</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>A character type.</p>
<p>The <code>char</code> type represents a single character. More specifically, since<br>
'character' isn't a well-defined concept in Unicode, <code>char</code> is a '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#unicode_scalar_value">Unicode<br>
scalar value</a>'.</p>
<p>This documentation describes a number of methods and trait implementations on the<br>
<code>char</code> type. For technical reasons, there is additional, separate<br>
documentation in <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/char/index.html">the <code>std::char</code> module</a> as well.</p>
<h1 id="validity-and-layout">Validity and Layout</h1>
<p>A <code>char</code> is a '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#unicode_scalar_value">Unicode scalar value</a>', which is any '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#code_point">Unicode code point</a>'<br>
other than a <a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_code_point">surrogate code point</a>. This has a fixed numerical definition:<br>
code points are in the range 0 to 0x10FFFF, inclusive.<br>
Surrogate code points, used by UTF-16, are in the range 0xD800 to 0xDFFF.</p>
<p>No <code>char</code> may be constructed, whether as a literal or at runtime, that is not a<br>
Unicode scalar value. Violating this rule causes undefined behavior.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Each of these is a compiler error
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{D800}&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{DFFF}&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{110000}&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Panics; from_u32 returns None.
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">from_u32</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mh">0xDE01</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">unwrap</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Undefined behavior
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">unsafe</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">from_u32_unchecked</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mh">0x110000</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Unicode scalar values are also the exact set of values that may be encoded in UTF-8. Because<br>
<code>char</code> values are Unicode scalar values and functions may assume <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/primitive.str.html#invariant">incoming <code>str</code> values are<br>
valid UTF-8</a>, it is safe to store any <code>char</code> in a <code>str</code> or read<br>
any character from a <code>str</code> as a <code>char</code>.</p>
<p>The gap in valid <code>char</code> values is understood by the compiler, so in the<br>
below example the two ranges are understood to cover the whole range of<br>
possible <code>char</code> values and there is no error for a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/book/ch06-02-match.html#matches-are-exhaustive">non-exhaustive match</a>.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">c</span>: <span class="kt">char</span> <span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;a&#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">match</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">c</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\0&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">..=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{D7FF}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">false</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{E000}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">..=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{10FFFF}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">true</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>All Unicode scalar values are valid <code>char</code> values, but not all of them represent a real<br>
character. Many Unicode scalar values are not currently assigned to a character, but may be in<br>
the future (&quot;reserved&quot;); some will never be a character (&quot;noncharacters&quot;); and some may be given<br>
different meanings by different users (&quot;private use&quot;).</p>
<p><code>char</code> is guaranteed to have the same size, alignment, and function call ABI as <code>u32</code> on all<br>
platforms.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">Layout</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">Layout</span>::<span class="n">new</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Layout</span>::<span class="n">new</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><h1 id="representation">Representation</h1>
<p><code>char</code> is always four bytes in size. This is a different representation than<br>
a given character would have as part of a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/string/struct.String.html"><code>String</code></a>. For example:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;h&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;e&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;l&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;l&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;o&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// five elements times four bytes for each element
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">20</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;hello&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// five elements times one byte per element
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>As always, remember that a human intuition for 'character' might not map to<br>
Unicode's definitions. For example, despite looking similar, the 'é'<br>
character is one Unicode code point while 'é' is two Unicode code points:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;é&#34;</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+00e9: &#39;latin small letter e with acute&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{00e9}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;é&#34;</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+0065: &#39;latin small letter e&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{0065}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+0301: &#39;combining acute accent&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{0301}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>This means that the contents of the first string above <em>will</em> fit into a<br>
<code>char</code> while the contents of the second string <em>will not</em>. Trying to create<br>
a <code>char</code> literal with the contents of the second string gives an error:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl">error: character literal may only contain one codepoint: &#39;é&#39;
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">let c = &#39;é&#39;;
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">        ^^^
</span></span></code></pre><p>Another implication of the 4-byte fixed size of a <code>char</code> is that<br>
per-<code>char</code> processing can end up using a lot more memory:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;love: ❤️&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span>: <span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">collect</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">12</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of_val</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="p">]));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">32</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of_val</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="p">]));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type.builtin">{`char`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ ->\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">option</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">enum</span> <span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="cm">/* … */</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>The <code>Option</code> type. See <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/option/index.html">the module level documentation</a> for more.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type">{`Option`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`<`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>The 8-bit unsigned integer type.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type.builtin">{`u8`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`>`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`let`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ res\ =\ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`match`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ op\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="string">{`'!'`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ =>\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>value of literal: <code>11 (0xB|0b1011)</code></p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="constant.builtin">{`11`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="string">{`'['`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ =>\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>value of literal: <code>11 (0xB|0b1011)</code></p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="constant.builtin">{`11`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ _\ =>\ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`return`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">option</span>::<span class="nb">Option</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="nb">None</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>No value.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="constructor">{`None`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`;`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">option</span>::<span class="nb">Option</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Some value of type <code>T</code>.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="constructor">{`Some`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`res`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

`}</span><span className="keyword">{`fn`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">infix_binding_power</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">op</span>: <span class="kt">char</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_148_3" className="function">{`infix_binding_power`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">op</span>: <span class="kt">char</span>
</span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>size = 4, align = 0x4, no Drop</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_148_23" className="variable.parameter">{`op`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`:`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">char</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>A character type.</p>
<p>The <code>char</code> type represents a single character. More specifically, since<br>
'character' isn't a well-defined concept in Unicode, <code>char</code> is a '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#unicode_scalar_value">Unicode<br>
scalar value</a>'.</p>
<p>This documentation describes a number of methods and trait implementations on the<br>
<code>char</code> type. For technical reasons, there is additional, separate<br>
documentation in <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/char/index.html">the <code>std::char</code> module</a> as well.</p>
<h1 id="validity-and-layout">Validity and Layout</h1>
<p>A <code>char</code> is a '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#unicode_scalar_value">Unicode scalar value</a>', which is any '<a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#code_point">Unicode code point</a>'<br>
other than a <a href="https://www.unicode.org/glossary/#surrogate_code_point">surrogate code point</a>. This has a fixed numerical definition:<br>
code points are in the range 0 to 0x10FFFF, inclusive.<br>
Surrogate code points, used by UTF-16, are in the range 0xD800 to 0xDFFF.</p>
<p>No <code>char</code> may be constructed, whether as a literal or at runtime, that is not a<br>
Unicode scalar value. Violating this rule causes undefined behavior.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Each of these is a compiler error
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{D800}&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{DFFF}&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{110000}&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Panics; from_u32 returns None.
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">from_u32</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mh">0xDE01</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">unwrap</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// Undefined behavior
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">_</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">unsafe</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kt">char</span>::<span class="n">from_u32_unchecked</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mh">0x110000</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Unicode scalar values are also the exact set of values that may be encoded in UTF-8. Because<br>
<code>char</code> values are Unicode scalar values and functions may assume <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/core/primitive.str.html#invariant">incoming <code>str</code> values are<br>
valid UTF-8</a>, it is safe to store any <code>char</code> in a <code>str</code> or read<br>
any character from a <code>str</code> as a <code>char</code>.</p>
<p>The gap in valid <code>char</code> values is understood by the compiler, so in the<br>
below example the two ranges are understood to cover the whole range of<br>
possible <code>char</code> values and there is no error for a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/book/ch06-02-match.html#matches-are-exhaustive">non-exhaustive match</a>.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">c</span>: <span class="kt">char</span> <span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;a&#39;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">match</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">c</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\0&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">..=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{D7FF}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">false</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{E000}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">..=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{10FFFF}&#39;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="kc">true</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>All Unicode scalar values are valid <code>char</code> values, but not all of them represent a real<br>
character. Many Unicode scalar values are not currently assigned to a character, but may be in<br>
the future (&quot;reserved&quot;); some will never be a character (&quot;noncharacters&quot;); and some may be given<br>
different meanings by different users (&quot;private use&quot;).</p>
<p><code>char</code> is guaranteed to have the same size, alignment, and function call ABI as <code>u32</code> on all<br>
platforms.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">alloc</span>::<span class="n">Layout</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">Layout</span>::<span class="n">new</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Layout</span>::<span class="n">new</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><h1 id="representation">Representation</h1>
<p><code>char</code> is always four bytes in size. This is a different representation than<br>
a given character would have as part of a <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/nightly/std/string/struct.String.html"><code>String</code></a>. For example:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="fm">vec!</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="sc">&#39;h&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;e&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;l&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;l&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="sc">&#39;o&#39;</span><span class="p">];</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// five elements times four bytes for each element
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">20</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;hello&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// five elements times one byte per element
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">5</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">len</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">*</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of</span>::<span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>As always, remember that a human intuition for 'character' might not map to<br>
Unicode's definitions. For example, despite looking similar, the 'é'<br>
character is one Unicode code point while 'é' is two Unicode code points:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;é&#34;</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+00e9: &#39;latin small letter e with acute&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{00e9}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;é&#34;</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+0065: &#39;latin small letter e&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{0065}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="c1">// U+0301: &#39;combining acute accent&#39;
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="sc">&#39;\\u{0301}&#39;</span><span class="p">),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">None</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">());</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>This means that the contents of the first string above <em>will</em> fit into a<br>
<code>char</code> while the contents of the second string <em>will not</em>. Trying to create<br>
a <code>char</code> literal with the contents of the second string gives an error:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl">error: character literal may only contain one codepoint: &#39;é&#39;
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">let c = &#39;é&#39;;
</span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl">        ^^^
</span></span></code></pre><p>Another implication of the 4-byte fixed size of a <code>char</code> is that<br>
per-<code>char</code> processing can end up using a lot more memory:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;love: ❤️&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">v</span>: <span class="nb">Vec</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">char</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">chars</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">collect</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">12</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of_val</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">s</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="p">]));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">32</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">size_of_val</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="n">v</span><span class="p">[</span><span class="o">..</span><span class="p">]));</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type.builtin">{`char`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ ->\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">option</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">enum</span> <span class="nb">Option</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>The <code>Option</code> type. See <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/option/index.html">the module level documentation</a> for more.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type">{`Option`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`<`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="w">

` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="type.builtin">{`u8`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kt">u8</span><span class="w">

`}</span><span className="attribute">{`#`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`[`}</span><span className="attribute">{`test`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`]`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
`}</span><span className="keyword">{`fn`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_161_3" className="function">{`tests`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`let`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ s\ =\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">expr</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">input</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">S</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_64_3" className="function">{`expr`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="string">{`"1"`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`;`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">assert_eq</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Asserts that two expressions are equal to each other (using <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/cmp/trait.PartialEq.html"><code>PartialEq</code></a>).</p>
<p>Assertions are always checked in both debug and release builds, and cannot<br>
be disabled. See [<code>debug_assert_eq!</code>] for assertions that are disabled in<br>
release builds by default.</p>
<p>On panic, this macro will print the values of the expressions with their<br>
debug representations.</p>
<p>Like <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/macros/builtin/macro.assert.html"><code>assert</code></a>, this macro has a second form, where a custom<br>
panic message can be provided.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">+</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;we are testing addition with {} and {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`assert_eq`}</span></Tooltip><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">assert_eq</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Asserts that two expressions are equal to each other (using <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/cmp/trait.PartialEq.html"><code>PartialEq</code></a>).</p>
<p>Assertions are always checked in both debug and release builds, and cannot<br>
be disabled. See [<code>debug_assert_eq!</code>] for assertions that are disabled in<br>
release builds by default.</p>
<p>On panic, this macro will print the values of the expressions with their<br>
debug representations.</p>
<p>Like <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/macros/builtin/macro.assert.html"><code>assert</code></a>, this macro has a second form, where a custom<br>
panic message can be provided.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">+</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Asserts that two expressions are equal to each other (using <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/cmp/trait.PartialEq.html"><code>PartialEq</code></a>).</p>
<p>Assertions are always checked in both debug and release builds, and cannot<br>
be disabled. See [<code>debug_assert_eq!</code>] for assertions that are disabled in<br>
release builds by default.</p>
<p>On panic, this macro will print the values of the expressions with their<br>
debug representations.</p>
<p>Like <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/macros/builtin/macro.assert.html"><code>assert</code></a>, this macro has a second form, where a custom<br>
panic message can be provided.</p>

</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">expr</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">input</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">S</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_64_3" className="function">{`expr`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="string">{`"\ 1\ +\ 2\ +\ f\ .\ g\ .\ h\ *\ 3\ *\ 4"`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`;`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">assert_eq</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #0
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Asserts that two expressions are equal to each other (using <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/cmp/trait.PartialEq.html"><code>PartialEq</code></a>).</p>
<p>Assertions are always checked in both debug and release builds, and cannot<br>
be disabled. See [<code>debug_assert_eq!</code>] for assertions that are disabled in<br>
release builds by default.</p>
<p>On panic, this macro will print the values of the expressions with their<br>
debug representations.</p>
<p>Like <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/macros/builtin/macro.assert.html"><code>assert</code></a>, this macro has a second form, where a custom<br>
panic message can be provided.</p>

\ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">

<p>Asserts that two expressions are equal to each other (using <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/cmp/trait.PartialEq.html"><code>PartialEq</code></a>).</p>

<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">3</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">1</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">+</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;we are testing addition with {} and {}&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">a</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">b</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`!`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`s`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`.`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`to_string`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="string">{`"(=\ a\ (=\ (?\ 0\ b\ c)\ d))"`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

`}</span><span className="keyword">{`fn`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span id="def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_209_3" className="function">{`main`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`for`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ line\ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`in`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ std`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`::`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`io`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`::`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">stdio</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">stdin</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">Stdin</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Constructs a new handle to the standard input of the current process.</p>
<p>Each handle returned is a reference to a shared global buffer whose access<br>
is synchronized via a mutex. If you need more explicit control over<br>
locking, see the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/stdio/struct.Stdin.html#method.lock"><code>Stdin::lock</code></a> method.</p>
<h3 id="note-windows-portability-considerations">Note: Windows Portability Considerations</h3>
<p>When operating in a console, the Windows implementation of this stream does not support<br>
non-UTF-8 byte sequences. Attempting to read bytes that are not valid UTF-8 will return<br>
an error.</p>
<p>In a process with a detached console, such as one using<br>
<code>#![windows_subsystem = &quot;windows&quot;]</code>, or in a child process spawned from such a process,<br>
the contained handle will be null. In such cases, the standard library's <code>Read</code> and<br>
<code>Write</code> will do nothing and silently succeed. All other I/O operations, via the<br>
standard library or via raw Windows API calls, will fail.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<p>Using implicit synchronization:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">main</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">io</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="p">()</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="p">{</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">buffer</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">new</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Using explicit synchronization:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">BufRead</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
