</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(())</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="p">}</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function">{`stdin`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`.`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="n">stdio</span>::<span class="n">Stdin</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">lock</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">StdinLock</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="nb">&#39;static</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Locks this handle to the standard input stream, returning a readable<br>
guard.</p>
<p>The lock is released when the returned lock goes out of scope. The<br>
returned guard also implements the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/trait.Read.html"><code>Read</code></a> and <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/trait.BufRead.html"><code>BufRead</code></a> traits for<br>
accessing the underlying data.</p>

</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">trait</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">BufRead</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">lines</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">Lines</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="bp">Self</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="c1">// Bounds from trait:
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="bp">Self</span>: <span class="nc">Read</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p><code>Self</code> = <code>StdinLock&lt;'_&gt;</code></p>
<hr>
<p>Returns an iterator over the lines of this reader.</p>
<p>The iterator returned from this function will yield instances of<br>
<code><br>
[io::Result]&lt;<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/string/struct.String.html">String</a>&gt;</code>. Each string returned will <em>not</em> have a newline<br>
byte (the <code>0xA</code> byte) or <code>CRLF</code> (<code>0xD</code>, <code>0xA</code> bytes) at the end.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<p><a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/cursor/struct.Cursor.html"><code>std::io::Cursor</code></a> is a type that implements <code>BufRead</code>. In<br>
this example, we use <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/cursor/struct.Cursor.html"><code>Cursor</code></a> to iterate over all the lines in a byte<br>
slice.</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">BufRead</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lines_iter</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">next</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Some</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nb">String</span>::<span class="n">from</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;lorem&#34;</span><span class="p">)));</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre><h1 id="errors">Errors</h1>
<p>Each line of the iterator has the same error semantics as <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/trait.BufRead.html#method.read_line"><code>BufRead::read_line</code></a>.</p>
` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="property">{`lines`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`{`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`let`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ line\ =\ line`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`.`}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">core</span>::<span class="n">result</span>::<span class="nb">Result</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">impl</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">E</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="n">T</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">E</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">pub</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">unwrap</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="bp">self</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">T</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">where</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">    </span><span class="n">E</span>: <span class="nc">fmt</span>::<span class="n">Debug</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p><code>T</code> = <code>String</code>, <code>E</code> = <code>Error</code></p>
<hr>
<p>Returns the contained <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/result/enum.Result.html#variant.Ok"><code>Ok</code></a> value, consuming the <code>self</code> value.</p>
<p>Because this function may panic, its use is generally discouraged.<br>
Panics are meant for unrecoverable errors, and<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/book/ch09-01-unrecoverable-errors-with-panic.html">may abort the entire program</a>.</p>
<p>Instead, prefer to use <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/book/ch09-02-recoverable-errors-with-result.html#a-shortcut-for-propagating-errors-the--operator">the <code>?</code> (try) operator</a>, or pattern matching<br>
to handle the <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/result/enum.Result.html#variant.Err"><code>Err</code></a> case explicitly, or call [<code>unwrap_or</code>],<br>
[<code>unwrap_or_else</code>], or [<code>unwrap_or_default</code>].</p>
<h1 id="panics">Panics</h1>
<p>Panics if the value is an <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/result/enum.Result.html#variant.Err"><code>Err</code></a>, with a panic message provided by the<br>
<a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/core/result/enum.Result.html#variant.Err"><code>Err</code></a>'s value.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<p>Basic usage:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span>: <span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Ok</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">assert_eq!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">unwrap</span><span class="p">(),</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">x</span>: <span class="nb">Result</span><span class="o">&lt;</span><span class="kt">u32</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="o">&gt;</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="nb">Err</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;emergency failure&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">x</span><span class="p">.</span><span class="n">unwrap</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// panics with \`emergency failure\`
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="property">{`unwrap`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`;`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="keyword">{`let`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ s\ =\ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">rs</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">fn</span> <span class="nf">expr</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">input</span>: <span class="kp">&amp;</span><span class="kt">str</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="w"> </span>-&gt; <span class="nc">S</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><a href="#def__Users_eric_Documents_Sources_cires_Eric_Song_Nop_github_io_rs_src_main_rs_64_3" className="function">{`expr`}</a></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="operator">{`&`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`line`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`;`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ `}</span><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">println</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #1
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Prints to the standard output, with a newline.</p>
<p>On all platforms, the newline is the LINE FEED character (<code>\\n</code>/<code>U+000A</code>) alone<br>
(no additional CARRIAGE RETURN (<code>\\r</code>/<code>U+000D</code>)).</p>
<p>This macro uses the same syntax as <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/macros/macro.format.html"><code>format</code></a>, but writes to the standard output instead.<br>
See [<code>std::fmt</code>] for more information.</p>
<p>The <code>println!</code> macro will lock the standard output on each call. If you call<br>
<code>println!</code> within a hot loop, this behavior may be the bottleneck of the loop.<br>
To avoid this, lock stdout with <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/stdio/struct.Stdout.html"><code>io::stdout().lock()</code></a>:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="n">stdout</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">lock</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">stdout</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">lock</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">writeln!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lock</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;hello world&#34;</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">unwrap</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Use <code>println!</code> only for the primary output of your program. Use<br>
[<code>eprintln!</code>] instead to print error and progress messages.</p>
<p>See the formatting documentation in <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/fmt/index.html"><code>std::fmt</code></a><br>
for details of the macro argument syntax.</p>
<h1 id="panics">Panics</h1>
<p>Panics if writing to [<code>io::stdout</code>] fails.</p>
<p>Writing to non-blocking stdout can cause an error, which will lead<br>
this macro to panic.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// prints just a newline
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;hello there!&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;format </span><span class="si">{}</span><span class="s"> arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;some&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">local_variable</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;some&#34;</span><span class="p">;</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;format </span><span class="si">{local_variable}</span><span class="s"> arguments&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`println`}</span></Tooltip><Tooltip overlay={<div className="cire-markdown" dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: `<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">macros</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="n">macro_rules</span><span class="o">!</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">println</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// matched arm #1
</span></span></span></code></pre><hr>
<p>Prints to the standard output, with a newline.</p>
<p>On all platforms, the newline is the LINE FEED character (<code>\\n</code>/<code>U+000A</code>) alone<br>
(no additional CARRIAGE RETURN (<code>\\r</code>/<code>U+000D</code>)).</p>
<p>This macro uses the same syntax as <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/macros/macro.format.html"><code>format</code></a>, but writes to the standard output instead.<br>
See [<code>std::fmt</code>] for more information.</p>
<p>The <code>println!</code> macro will lock the standard output on each call. If you call<br>
<code>println!</code> within a hot loop, this behavior may be the bottleneck of the loop.<br>
To avoid this, lock stdout with <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/std/io/stdio/struct.Stdout.html"><code>io::stdout().lock()</code></a>:</p>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="k">use</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">std</span>::<span class="n">io</span>::<span class="p">{</span><span class="n">stdout</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">Write</span><span class="p">};</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="kd">let</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="k">mut</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">lock</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="o">=</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="n">stdout</span><span class="p">().</span><span class="n">lock</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">writeln!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="n">lock</span><span class="p">,</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="s">&#34;hello world&#34;</span><span class="p">).</span><span class="n">unwrap</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w">
</span></span></span></code></pre><p>Use <code>println!</code> only for the primary output of your program. Use<br>
[<code>eprintln!</code>] instead to print error and progress messages.</p>
<p>See the formatting documentation in <a href="https://doc.rust-lang.org/stable/alloc/fmt/index.html"><code>std::fmt</code></a><br>
for details of the macro argument syntax.</p>
<h1 id="panics">Panics</h1>
<p>Panics if writing to [<code>io::stdout</code>] fails.</p>
<p>Writing to non-blocking stdout can cause an error, which will lead<br>
this macro to panic.</p>
<h1 id="examples">Examples</h1>
<pre class="chroma"><code><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">();</span><span class="w"> </span><span class="c1">// prints just a newline
</span></span></span><span class="line"><span class="cl"><span class="fm">println!</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s">&#34;hello there!&#34;</span><span class="p">);</span><span class="w">

</span></span></span></code></pre>` }} />} placement="top" trigger={['hover']}><span className="function.macro">{`!`}</span></Tooltip><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`(`}</span><span className="string">{`"{}"`}</span><span className="punctuation.delimiter">{`,`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`\ s`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`)`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
\ \ \ \ `}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`
`}</span><span className="punctuation.bracket">{`}`}</span><span className="cire_text">{`

`}</span></code></pre>
